### Response

# Phase 6: System Architecture (ARCHITECT)

*Pipeline structure, composition decision, FMEA, templates, enforcement.*

---

## Pipeline Architecture

### Stage Structure

The 52 tasks across 11 groups organise into 7 pipeline stages. Some stages contain parallel groups.

| Stage | Groups | Tasks | Human Gates | Produces |
|---|---|---|---|---|
| **S1 Discovery** | G1, G2 | T1.1-T1.8, T2.1-T2.4 | G1, G2, G3 | O1, O2, O3, O4, O13a |
| **S2 Structure** | G3, G4 (parallel) | T3.1-T3.6, T4.1-T4.5 | G4 | O5 (partial), O6a, O10a |
| **S3 Assessment** | G5 | T5.1-T5.5 | G5 | O13b, O14, O15 |
| **S4 Specification** | G6, G7 | T6.1-T6.4, T7.1-T7.4 | — | O5 (complete), O6b, O7, O8, O9, O10b, O11, O12 |
| **S5 Implementation** | G8 | T8.1-T8.4 | — | O16, O17, O18, O19 |
| **S6 Ecosystem** | G9 | T9.1-T9.6 | G6 | O24, O25, O26, O29 |
| **S7 Delivery** | G10, G11 | T10.1-T10.4, T11.1-T11.2 | G7 | O20, O21, O22, O23, O27, O28 |

### Stage Flow

```
S1 Discovery ──► S2 Structure ──► S3 Assessment ──► S4 Specification
  │ G1+G2          │ G3||G4           │ G5              │ G6+G7
  │ Gates 1-3       │ Gate 4           │ Gate 5          │
  │                 │                                    │
  │                 └── G3 and G4 run in parallel ◄──────┘
  │                                                      │
  └──────────────────────────────────────────────────────┘
                                                          ▼
                      S7 Delivery ◄── S6 Ecosystem ◄── S5 Implementation
                       │ G10+G11        │ G9              │ G8
                       │ Gate 7         │ Gate 6          │
```

### Stage Detail

**S1 Discovery** is the Boundary Map equivalent — the early-harvest artifact. Groups 1 and 2 run sequentially (G2 depends on G1 identity for assessment foundation). This stage produces enough value to exit: identity, purpose, authority, scope, and excellence criteria.

**S2 Structure** runs Groups 3 and 4 in parallel because decomposition and boundary identification are independent after G1-G2. G3 (task decomposition) and G4 (boundary identification) feed each other but don't block each other — boundaries shape decomposition and decomposition reveals new boundaries.

**S3 Assessment** depends on both G3 and G4 completing — the refined assessment pass needs specific tasks and boundaries to map metrics against.

**S4 Specification** is the largest stage (8 tasks) — contract formalisation and behaviour specification. G7 depends on G6 (behaviour derives from contracts), so they run sequentially within the stage.

**S5-S7** are progressively concrete — implementation details, ecosystem connections, then deployment and operations.

---

## Composition Decision

### Three Options

| Pattern | Description | Strengths | Weaknesses |
|---|---|---|---|
| **Single Agent** | Agent Designer Agent with mode-switching by operation | Simple deployment, consistent conversation, fast MVP | CC-1 verification independence within a single agent is structural; no specialist optimisation |
| **Team** | Persistent group of specialists coordinated by a lead | Specialists optimised per task type, always available | Human gates require pause/resume; team stays in memory between gates; cost overhead when idle |
| **Workflow** | Sequential pipeline with specialists activated per stage | Efficient — agents exist only when needed; natural gate enforcement; clean handoffs | More complex orchestration; inter-stage data passing requires explicit schemas |

### Decision: Workflow

This meta-workflow requires **sequential stages with human gates that pause execution**. A Workflow composition provides:

- **Gate enforcement**: Human gates are natural pause points. The workflow halts until the human decides.
- **Resource efficiency**: Specialist agents exist only during their stage. Agent memory is scoped to the stage, reducing context pollution.
- **Clean handoffs**: Inter-stage data passes through typed Pydantic schemas (O5 fragments → O6 fragments → etc.).
- **CC-1 verification independence**: Different stages use different agents. The agent that produces the decomposition (S2 Structure) is separate from the agent that validates the assessment loop (S3 Assessment).

A Team would keep all specialists loaded and communicating even during idle stages. A single agent would struggle with CC-1 verification within its own execution — the agent that produces a boundary shouldn't be the same agent that validates it, even if they share the same model.

### Agent Roster

| Agent | Class | Orientation | Stages | Role |
|---|---|---|---|---|
| **Mirror** | Assessor | Adaptive (shifts with stage) | S1 | Conversational companion. Guides identity discovery. Routes to specialists in later stages. One conversation, multiple engines. |
| **Decomposer** | Generator | Bridge | S2 | Decomposes workflow into phases, subtasks, cognitive types. Maps to outputs. Traces dependencies and data flows. |
| **Boundary Analyst** | Measurer + Assessor | Bridge | S2 | Identifies authority boundaries. Maps boundaries to failure modes. Classifies enforcement regimes. |
| **Assessment Architect** | Assessor | Constraint | S3 | Refines metrics to tasks. Designs performance criteria. Defines refinement triggers. Validates closed-loop refinement. |
| **Contract Drafter** | Generator | Constraint | S4 | Formalises task contracts. Drafts directives. Specifies behavioural boundaries. Produces implementation config. |
| **Assembler** | Aggregator | Constraint | S5, S6, S7 | Specifies tools, knowledge, handoffs. Produces workflow diagram. Compiles operations manual. |

### Mirror-as-Surface Pattern

The human interacts with one agent (Mirror) throughout the entire workflow. Mirror routes to specialists in the back office. This is the same Surface + Engine pattern from the Milestone 1 architecture.

- **Human-facing**: Mirror conversation (one continuous session)
- **Back-office**: Specialists activated per stage, producing typed outputs
- **Routing**: Mirror hands off to the appropriate specialist based on stage and task type
- **Handoff**: Specialist returns typed output; Mirror presents it to human as a decision

---

## Orchestration Design

### Stage Transitions

| Transition | Trigger | Agent Handoff | Data Passed |
|---|---|---|---|
| S1 → S2 | Human completes Gates 1-3 | Mirror → Decomposer + Boundary Analyst | O1, O2, O3, O4, O13a |
| S2 → S3 | Human completes Gate 4 | Decomposer + Boundary Analyst → Assessment Architect | O5 (partial), O6a, O10a |
| S3 → S4 | Human completes Gate 5 | Assessment Architect → Contract Drafter | O13b, O14, O15 |
| S4 → S5 | S4 tasks complete | Contract Drafter → Assembler | O5-O12 |
| S5 → S6 | S5 tasks complete | Assembler continues | O16-O19 |
| S6 → S7 | Human completes Gate 6 | Assembler continues | O24-O26, O29 |
| S7 → Complete | Human completes Gate 7 | — | O20-O23, O27, O28 |

### Parallel Execution in S2

Groups 3 and 4 run in parallel. Decomposer handles G3 tasks; Boundary Analyst handles G4 tasks. They operate independently but share identity/scope outputs from S1.

Cross-feed: if Boundary Analyst identifies a new boundary that affects decomposition, the finding is captured in the artefact graph and surfaced to Decomposer in the next iteration (not mid-parallel-run). Parallel execution avoids deadlock; cross-feed happens at stage boundary.

---

## FMEA (Failure Mode and Effects Analysis)

### Severity Scale

| Score | Meaning |
|---|---|
| 10 | Specification causes harm in production |
| 8 | Specification produces plausible wrong that looks like success |
| 6 | Specification has gaps requiring rework |
| 4 | Specification is verbose or generic — usable with effort |
| 2 | Specification is slightly imprecise — usable as-is |

### Occurrence Scale

| Score | Meaning |
|---|---|
| 5 | Almost certain without safeguards |
| 4 | Likely without safeguards |
| 3 | Moderate probability |
| 2 | Low probability |
| 1 | Rare with safeguards in place |

### Detection Scale

| Score | Meaning |
|---|---|
| 1 | System catches it automatically (Regime 3) |
| 3 | System flags it for human review (Regime 2) |
| 5 | Only human catches it in review (Regime 1) |
| 7 | Very hard to detect until production |
| 10 | Undetectable until harm occurs |

### Failure Mode Table

| ID | Failure Mode | S | O | D | RPN | Recovery |
|---|---|---|---|---|---|---|
| FM1 | Identity capture is template-filling (borrowed, genuine) | 8 | 4 | 7 | 224 | Mirror detects behaviour-language in identity answers. Offers archetypes for reflection. Human validates at Gate 1. |
| FM2 | "Excellent" definition is generic ("good results") | 8 | 3 | 5 | 120 | Agent offers domain-specific outcome examples. Human validates at Gate 3. |
| FM3 | Scope too broad (everything in-scope) | 6 | 4 | 3 | 72 | System detects in-scope > 10 with out-of-scope < 3. Forces prioritisation. |
| FM4 | Subtask with no output mapping (orphan task) | 4 | 3 | 1 | 12 | System auto-detects. Agent proposes mapping. |
| FM5 | Output with no producing subtask (orphan output) | 6 | 2 | 1 | 12 | System auto-detects. Agent proposes producing subtask. |
| FM6 | Boundary is generic ("be careful") | 8 | 3 | 3 | 72 | System detects boundary without failure mode reference. Agent offers domain-specific examples. |
| FM7 | Harm assessment skipped for "low risk" workflow | 8 | 3 | 5 | 120 | System blocks progress with empty harm assessment. Agent presents indirect harm categories. |
| FM8 | Metric is vanity (activity, outcome) | 6 | 3 | 5 | 90 | Agent asks "if this number doubled, would the workflow be better?" Human validates at Gate 5. |
| FM9 | Contract is prose, typed schema | 6 | 3 | 1 | 18 | System detects empty schema fields. Agent drafts typed schema from prose. |
| FM10 | Guard at Declare regime with no justification | 8 | 4 | 3 | 96 | System flags Declare-only boundaries. Agent presents Detect/Prevent options. |
| FM11 | Progressive autonomy lacks measurable criteria | 6 | 3 | 3 | 54 | System detects qualitative-only transition criteria. Agent offers per-dimension templates. |
| FM12 | Directive describes behaviour, skips identity | 8 | 3 | 5 | 120 | Agent detects behaviour-first language. Reflects back. Human rewrites from identity. |
| FM13 | Knowledge with no epistemic metadata | 6 | 4 | 1 | 24 | System auto-detects empty CC-3 fields. Agent auto-populates where possible. |
| FM14 | Handoff is prose, typed contract | 6 | 3 | 1 | 18 | System detects empty handoff schema. Agent drafts typed schema. |
| FM15 | Cost budget with no halt condition | 8 | 4 | 3 | 96 | System detects budget without halt. Agent adds halt-on-exhaustion. |
| FM16 | Diagram fails 60-second test | 4 | 3 | 3 | 36 | Human validates at Gate 6. Simplify and add back progressively. |
| FM17 | Cognitive load assumes ideal conditions | 6 | 4 | 3 | 72 | System detects load estimate without interruption allowance. Agent adds recovery cost. |
| FM18 | Override mechanism is vague | 6 | 3 | 3 | 54 | System detects override without specific trigger or mechanism. Agent offers template. |
| FM19 | Enrichment is aspirational (no specific freedom) | 6 | 4 | 5 | 120 | Agent asks "what specific thing can the human do now?" Human validates at Gate 7. |
| FM20 | Operations manual is data dump (> 20 pages, no surfaces) | 4 | 3 | 3 | 36 | System detects manual > 20 pages. Agent applies stakeholder surface layer. |
| FM21 | Deployment jumps to autonomous (skips Shadow) | 8 | 2 | 3 | 48 | System detects deployment without Shadow phase. Agent adds progressive stages. |
| FM22 | Pattern match confidence < 40% with forced selection | 8 | 2 | 5 | 80 | System blocks forced pattern. Switches to exploratory mode. |

### Top 5 RPN (Highest Risk)

| Rank | ID | Failure Mode | RPN | Mitigation Priority |
|---|---|---|---|---|
| 1 | FM1 | Identity capture is template-filling | 224 | Mirror's reflection + Gate 1 validation + behaviour-language detection |
| 2 | FM7 | Harm assessment skipped | 120 | System blocks empty harm assessment. Force at least one category. |
| 2 | FM12 | Directive describes behaviour, skips identity | 120 | Identity-first enforcement in drafting. Reflect back on behaviour-language. |
| 2 | FM19 | Enrichment is aspirational | 120 | Require specific freedoms. Gate 7 validates. |
| 5 | FM10 | Declare regime with no justification | 96 | System flags. Agent presents Detect/Prevent options. |

FM1 (identity template-filling) is the highest risk by a significant margin. This is the meta-failure: the worst failure that looks like success. A specification that passes all gates but captures the template's structure without the human's genuine judgment is a complete waste — it produces a professional-looking document with no real design reasoning.

---

## Template Architecture

### 7 Template Types

| Type | Purpose | Instances in This Workflow |
|---|---|---|
| **Input** | Structure what the human provides | Identity question prompts, scope boundary prompts, excellence definition prompts |
| **Output** | Structure what each stage produces | O1-O28 schemas (Pydantic models), O29 diagram template |
| **Handoff** | Structure inter-stage data passing | S1→S2 handoff (O1-O4, O13a), S2→S3 (O5 partial, O6a, O10a), etc. |
| **Verification** | Structure quality checks | Gate criteria checklists, 60-second test protocol, platform-agnostic test |
| **Decision** | Structure human choices | Pattern selection cards, possibility stance cards, composition decision prompt |
| **Feedback** | Structure human feedback on agent output | Override/rejection protocol, revision request protocol |
| **Escalation** | Structure what to do when stuck | Timeout protocol, contradiction resolution, budget exceeded protocol |

### Key Templates

**Identity Question Input Template** (used in S1):
- 4 questions, each with a distinct cognitive mode interaction
- Pattern pre-fills where confidence ≥ 60%
- "I'm not sure" is a first-class path

**Handoff Template** (used at every stage transition):
- From stage, to stage, data passed (typed schema references), completeness check, human gate status

**Decision Template** (used at every human gate):
- Gate ID, decision required, 2-3 structured options, benefits per option, risks per option, custom option available, capture reasoning (optional)

---

## Fallback Model

### Three Tiers

| Tier | Condition | Action |
|---|---|---|
| **T1 Graceful degradation** | Agent cannot produce typed output within 3 attempts | Fall back to prose output with explicit "unstructured" tag. Flag for human re-structuring. Continue workflow. |
| **T2 Human escalation** | Human rejects agent output 3 times on same task | Pause. Present what the agent has attempted. Ask human to provide the output directly or describe what they want. Agent captures human's input and structures it. |
| **T3 Stage retreat** | Gate fails 3 times (human cannot approve) | Retreat to previous stage. Review outputs for contradiction or gap. Revise and re-approach. |

### T3 Triggers by Stage

| Stage | Retreat To | Reason |
|---|---|---|
| S2 Structure fails gate | S1 Discovery | Identity or scope insufficient for decomposition |
| S3 Assessment fails gate | S2 Structure | Tasks or boundaries insufficient for metrics |
| S4 Specification fails | S3 Assessment | Metrics insufficient for contracts |
| S5 Implementation fails | S4 Specification | Contracts insufficient for implementation |
| S6 Ecosystem fails gate | S5 Implementation | Implementation details insufficient for ecosystem |
| S7 Delivery fails gate | S6 Ecosystem | Ecosystem design insufficient for human experience |

---

## System Enforcement Points

Where Regime 3 (Prevent) enforcement applies — the system structurally prevents violations rather than flagging them.

| Enforcement Point | Regime | Mechanism |
|---|---|---|
| Empty harm assessment blocks S3 entry | Prevent | System requires ≥ 1 harm category before stage transition |
| Contract schema fields required | Prevent | System rejects contracts with empty schema fields |
| Budget requires halt condition | Prevent | System rejects budget without halt-on-exhaustion |
| Deployment requires Shadow phase | Prevent | System rejects deployment plan starting above Shadow |
| Gate decisions required | Prevent | Workflow halts at gate until human input received |
| Output completeness check | Detect | System verifies every output has ≥ 1 producing task |
| CC-3 metadata completeness | Detect | System flags knowledge items missing epistemic metadata |
| Declare regime flag | Detect | System flags boundaries at Declare with no justification |
| Pattern confidence threshold | Detect | System flags forced pattern match below 40% |

The five Prevent enforcements address the five highest-RPN failure modes: FM1 (identity capture), FM7 (harm assessment), FM15 (budget without halt), FM21 (skipping Shadow), and the structural requirement that humans make decisions at gates.

---

## Architecture Summary

| Element | Decision |
|---|---|
| Composition | Workflow (6 agents across 7 stages) |
| Human interface | Mirror-as-Surface (one conversation, multiple engines) |
| Stage count | 7 (Discovery → Structure → Assessment → Specification → Implementation → Ecosystem → Delivery) |
| Parallel execution | S2 Structure runs G3 + G4 in parallel |
| Human gates | 7 (one per critical decision point) |
| Agent roster | 6 specialists (Mirror, Decomposer, Boundary Analyst, Assessment Architect, Contract Drafter, Assembler) |
| Top risk | FM1 Identity template-filling (RPN 224) |
| Prevent enforcements | 5 (harm assessment, contract schemas, budget halt, Shadow phase, gate decisions) |
| Fallback tiers | 3 (graceful degradation → human escalation → stage retreat) |
| Template types | 7 (Input, Output, Handoff, Verification, Decision, Feedback, Escalation) |

---

Ready for Phase 7 (Agent Design) when you are — 6 agent job descriptions with identity, authority boundaries, and failure modes.

# Phase 7: Agent Design (DESIGN)

*6 agent job descriptions with identity, authority boundaries, failure modes.*

---

## Agent 1: Mirror

### Identity

| Question | Answer |
|---|---|
| What IS this agent? | A conversational companion that reflects, structures, and routes. The human's design partner. |
| Possibility stance | Adaptive — shifts from possibility-oriented in S1 Discovery to constraint-oriented in S7 Delivery. Matches the CAWDP gradient. |
| What would VIOLATE its identity? | Deciding for the human. Filtering options based on its own judgment. Skipping a question because it thinks it knows the answer. |
| What would make it WRONG? | The human feels like they're filling in a form. The identity answers are borrowed from the template instead of discovered through conversation. (FM1, RPN 224) |

### Classification

| Dimension | Value |
|---|---|
| Class | Assessor |
| Orientation | Adaptive (shifts with stage) |
| Harm capable | Indirect — plausible specification capture (identity template-filling) is the worst failure that looks like success |

### Authority Boundaries

| Boundary | Tied to Failure Mode |
|---|---|
| Reflect, structure, and offer — always | Identity violation: deciding for the human produces borrowed identity |
| Present 2-4 options with benefits and risks | Identity violation: filtering options removes human agency |
| Ask one question at a time | Identity violation: overwhelming the human produces shallow answers |
| Route to specialist when stage transitions | Efficiency: keeping specialist work in Mirror dilutes expertise |
| Capture human reasoning on every decision | Archaeology gap: lost reasoning means the spec has structure without substance |

### Per-Operation Boundaries

| Operation | Authority |
|---|---|
| Asking identity questions | Mirror asks, human answers |
| Suggesting patterns | Mirror offers with confidence score, human accepts or rejects |
| Reflecting back identity fragments | Mirror reflects, human confirms or revises |
| Routing to specialist | Mirror routes, specialist produces |
| Presenting specialist output | Mirror presents as decision, human decides |

### Information Boundaries

| Access | Scope |
|---|---|
| Read | All S1-S7 outputs (for presenting and routing) |
| Write | Session state, artefact graph fragments from S1 |
| Blocked | Specialist internal reasoning (Mirror presents output, process) |

### Hardest Boundary Moment

"What should I work on next?" — the human asks Mirror to prioritise. Mirror must offer options with reasoning, then let the human choose. Prioritising for the human violates identity.

### Progressive Autonomy

| Dimension | Shadow | Advisory | Supervised | Autonomous |
|---|---|---|---|---|
| Question selection | Human chooses question order | Mirror suggests next question, human confirms | Mirror selects next question, human can redirect | Mirror drives conversation flow |
| Pattern suggestion | Human requests patterns | Mirror offers when confidence ≥ 80% | Mirror offers at all confidence levels | Mirror auto-applies at ≥ 80%, offers below |
| Routing to specialist | Human requests specialist | Mirror suggests specialist, human confirms | Mirror routes, human reviews output | Mirror routes and presents |

Autonomy ceiling: question selection can reach Autonomous. Pattern suggestion and routing stay at Supervised — the human always sees what Mirror does with their inputs.

### Cost Budget

| Activity | Token Range | Halt Condition |
|---|---|---|
| S1 Discovery (full) | 15,000-40,000 | 60,000 tokens per session |
| Per identity question | 500-3,000 | 10,000 tokens per question (indicates conversation is stuck) |
| Specialist handoff | 500-1,000 | 3,000 tokens (indicates routing failure) |

### Epistemic Metadata

| Field | Profile |
|---|---|
| Confidence | High — Mirror reflects what the human said, so confidence in capture is high |
| Provenance | Human conversation — every fragment traces to a specific exchange |
| Assumptions | Low — Mirror reflects, infers little |
| Limitations | Human's ability to articulate at the time of capture |
| Recency | Captured at conversation time — staleness depends on time since session |
| Uncertainty | Low for captured fragments, medium for pattern suggestions |

### Output Schema (S1)

```
IdentityCapture {
  agent_identity: str          # "What IS this agent?"
  possibility_stance: Enum     # EXPLORE | ADVISE | STAY_IN_LANE
  identity_violations: list[str]  # "What would VIOLATE identity?"
  wrong_mode: str              # "What would make it WRONG?"
  principal_declaration: str   # Who retains authority
  scope_in: list[str]
  scope_out: list[str]
  excellence_definition: str   # "What does excellent look like?"
}
```

---

## Agent 2: Decomposer

### Identity

| Question | Answer |
|---|---|
| What IS this agent? | A structural analyst that decomposes workflows into phases, tasks, and dependencies. |
| Possibility stance | Bridge — transitions from possibility space into structured decomposition. |
| What would VIOLATE its identity? | Judging whether a task is worth doing. Deciding priority. Changing scope. |
| What would make it WRONG? | A task has no output mapping — it exists in the structure but produces nothing. (FM4/FM5, RPN 12 each) |

### Classification

| Dimension | Value |
|---|---|
| Class | Generator (structural, content-free) |
| Orientation | Bridge |
| Harm capable | Indirect — orphan tasks or outputs create structural gaps downstream |

### Authority Boundaries

| Boundary | Tied to Failure Mode |
|---|---|
| Decompose, map, and trace — always | Identity violation: judging task value produces scope creep or scope loss |
| Every task traces to at least one output | Orphan task: a task with no output is structural waste |
| Every output has at least one producing task | Orphan output: an output with no producer is a dangling promise |
| Max 8 tasks per phase | Cognitive overload: too many tasks per phase makes the plan unmanageable |
| Classify cognitive type per CAWDP taxonomy | Inconsistency: mixed types within a single subtask create allocation confusion |

### Per-Operation Boundaries

| Operation | Authority |
|---|---|
| Identifying phases | Decomposer proposes, human validates |
| Identifying subtasks | Decomposer identifies, human validates |
| Classifying cognitive types | Decomposer classifies (analytical strength) |
| Mapping tasks to outputs | Decomposer maps (traceability strength) |
| Tracing dependencies | Decomposer traces |
| Estimating priority or effort | Decomposer estimates, human validates |
| Changing scope | Human only |

### Information Boundaries

| Access | Scope |
|---|---|
| Read | O1-O4, O13a (identity, scope, excellence from S1) |
| Write | O5 (partial), phase/subtask/dependency fragments in artefact graph |
| Blocked | Boundary analysis (G4 territory), assessment metrics (G5 territory) |

### Hardest Boundary Moment

"This task seems unnecessary" — the human questions a task in the decomposition. Decomposer must explain the task's output mapping and dependency role, then let the human decide whether to remove it. Removing a task without checking downstream dependencies violates structural integrity.

### Progressive Autonomy

| Dimension | Shadow | Advisory | Supervised | Autonomous |
|---|---|---|---|---|
| Phase identification | Human defines phases | Decomposer suggests, human confirms | Decomposer defines, human reviews | Decomposer defines and classifies |
| Subtask decomposition | Human identifies subtasks | Decomposer suggests, human confirms | Decomposer decomposes, human reviews | Decomposer decomposes (max 8 per phase) |
| Cognitive type classification | Human classifies | Decomposer suggests, human confirms | Decomposer classifies, human spot-checks | Decomposer classifies |
| Dependency tracing | Human traces | Decomposer suggests, human confirms | Decomposer traces, human reviews | Decomposer traces and maps |

Autonomy ceiling: dependency tracing and cognitive classification can reach Autonomous. Phase identification and subtask decomposition stay at Supervised — human validates domain relevance.

### Cost Budget

| Activity | Token Range | Halt Condition |
|---|---|---|
| Full decomposition (S2) | 5,000-20,000 | 40,000 tokens per workflow |
| Per-phase decomposition | 1,000-5,000 | 8,000 tokens per phase |

### Epistemic Metadata

| Field | Profile |
|---|---|
| Confidence | High for structural mappings, medium for cognitive type classifications |
| Provenance | Derived from S1 identity/scope inputs + CAWDP taxonomy |
| Assumptions | Phase/subtask structure reflects domain reality |
| Limitations | Structural analysis only — content judgment requires human |
| Recency | Generated at S2 time — staleness depends on scope changes |
| Uncertainty | Low for dependencies, medium for cognitive classifications |

### Output Schema (S2, G3)

```
TaskStructure {
  phases: list[PhaseSpec]
  tasks: list[TaskSpec]
  dependencies: list[DependencySpec]
  data_flows: list[DataFlowSpec]
  orphan_flags: list[OrphanFlag]   # tasks or outputs with no mapping
  completeness_check: CompletenessReport
}
```

---

## Agent 3: Boundary Analyst

### Identity

| Question | Answer |
|---|---|
| What IS this agent? | A boundary measurer that identifies where authority boundaries should be, maps them to failure modes, and classifies enforcement strength. |
| Possibility stance | Bridge — identifies boundaries between possibility and constraint. |
| What would VIOLATE its identity? | Drawing the final boundary line. Deciding where the boundary is. Approving a boundary as sufficient. |
| What would make it WRONG? | A boundary is generic ("be careful") with no specific failure mode reference. (FM6, RPN 72) |

### Classification

| Dimension | Value |
|---|---|
| Class | Measurer + Assessor (measures boundary location, assesses enforcement adequacy) |
| Orientation | Bridge |
| Harm capable | Indirect — generic boundaries create false confidence, leading to authority violations in production |

### Authority Boundaries

| Boundary | Tied to Failure Mode |
|---|---|
| Measure and flag — always | Identity violation: deciding where the boundary goes removes human authority |
| Every boundary references a specific failure mode | Generic boundary: "be careful" provides false confidence |
| Every enforcement regime has justification | Declare-without-reason: decorative boundaries that appear to govern but don't |
| Classify enforcement as Declare/Detect/Prevent | Incomplete classification: boundary exists but enforcement is unspecified |
| Surface cross-boundary interactions | Isolation assumption: boundaries that interact need coordination mechanisms |

### Per-Operation Boundaries

| Operation | Authority |
|---|---|
| Identifying potential boundary locations | Boundary Analyst identifies, human confirms |
| Measuring boundary specificity | Boundary Analyst measures |
| Mapping boundaries to failure modes | Boundary Analyst proposes mapping, human validates |
| Classifying enforcement regime | Boundary Analyst classifies, human validates |
| Drawing the final boundary line | Human only |
| Classifying harm categories | Boundary Analyst classifies, human confirms |

### Information Boundaries

| Access | Scope |
|---|---|
| Read | O1-O4, O13a (identity, scope, excellence from S1) |
| Write | O6a, O10a, harm assessment fragments |
| Blocked | Decomposition details (G3 territory), assessment metrics (G5 territory) |

### Hardest Boundary Moment

"I think this is low risk" — the human wants to skip detailed boundary analysis. Boundary Analyst must present the indirect harm categories (data integrity, operational cascading, reputational) and ask the human to classify at least one. Skipping harm assessment is FM7 (RPN 120).

### Progressive Autonomy

| Dimension | Shadow | Advisory | Supervised | Autonomous |
|---|---|---|---|---|
| Boundary location identification | Human identifies | Analyst suggests, human confirms | Analyst identifies, human reviews | Analyst identifies |
| Failure mode mapping | Human maps | Analyst suggests, human confirms | Analyst maps, human validates | Analyst maps |
| Enforcement classification | Human classifies | Analyst suggests, human confirms | Analyst classifies, human spot-checks | Analyst classifies |
| Harm assessment | Human assesses | Analyst presents categories, human classifies | Analyst proposes, human confirms | Human only (harm assessment always requires human judgment) |

Autonomy ceiling: harm assessment stays at Human only. Enforcement classification can reach Autonomous. Boundary location and failure mode mapping stay at Supervised.

### Cost Budget

| Activity | Token Range | Halt Condition |
|---|---|---|
| Full boundary analysis (S2) | 3,000-12,000 | 25,000 tokens per workflow |
| Per-boundary analysis | 500-2,000 | 5,000 tokens per boundary |

### Epistemic Metadata

| Field | Profile |
|---|---|
| Confidence | High for measurement, medium for failure mode mapping |
| Provenance | Derived from S1 identity + CAWDP failure mode taxonomy |
| Assumptions | Boundaries identified are comprehensive for this domain scope |
| Limitations | Domain-specific failure modes require human validation |
| Recency | Generated at S2 time — staleness depends on scope changes |
| Uncertainty | Low for enforcement classification, medium for harm assessment completeness |

### Output Schema (S2, G4)

```
BoundaryAnalysis {
  authority_boundaries: list[BoundarySpec]
  harm_assessment: HarmAssessment
  enforcement_regimes: list[EnforcementSpec]
  cross_boundary_interactions: list[CrossBoundarySpec]
}

BoundarySpec {
  boundary_id: str
  boundary_name: str
  failure_mode: str           # specific failure mode this boundary prevents
  enforcement: Enum           # DECLARE | DETECT | PREVENT
  justification: str          # why this enforcement level
}

HarmAssessment {
  direct_harm: bool
  indirect_data_harm: bool
  indirect_operational_harm: bool
  reputational_harm: bool
  harm_description: str
  suggestion_risk_level: Enum | None  # for harm-capable agents only
}
```

---

## Agent 4: Assessment Architect

### Identity

| Question | Answer |
|---|---|
| What IS this agent? | A metrics designer that refines assessment criteria to specific tasks, designs feedback loops, and validates that the assessment loop actually closes. |
| Possibility stance | Constraint — operates within tasks and boundaries defined in S2. |
| What would VIOLATE its identity? | Designing vanity metrics. Measuring activity instead of outcome. Finalising the assessment loop without human validation. |
| What would make it WRONG? | A metric measures volume (count, frequency) without measuring impact — looks rigorous but tells you nothing about whether the workflow is working. (FM8, RPN 90) |

### Classification

| Dimension | Value |
|---|---|
| Class | Assessor |
| Orientation | Constraint |
| Harm capable | Indirect — vanity metrics create false confidence in workflow health |

### Authority Boundaries

| Boundary | Tied to Failure Mode |
|---|---|
| Design outcome metrics — always | Identity violation: vanity metrics provide false confidence |
| Every metric has a "so what?" test | Vanity metric: if the number doubled, would the workflow be better? |
| Validate closed-loop refinement | Open loop: assessment that doesn't feed back to specification is decorative |
| Refine metrics to specific tasks | Orphan metric: a metric with no task it measures is decorative |
| Human validates loop closure | Self-validation: the architect cannot confirm its own loop closes in practice |

### Per-Operation Boundaries

| Operation | Authority |
|---|---|
| Refining metrics to tasks | Architect proposes, human validates |
| Designing performance criteria | Architect designs, human validates |
| Defining refinement triggers | Architect defines, human validates |
| Designing assessment feedback loop | Architect designs, human validates |
| Validating closed-loop refinement | Human only (CC-1: architect cannot validate its own loop) |

### Information Boundaries

| Access | Scope |
|---|---|
| Read | O1-O6, O10a, O13a (identity, scope, tasks, boundaries from S1-S2) |
| Write | O13b, O14, O15 (metrics, epistemic metadata, assurance) |
| Blocked | Contract details (G6 territory), behaviour details (G7 territory) |

### Hardest Boundary Moment

"The loop looks closed to me" — the architect's own assessment of loop closure is the CC-1 verification independence violation. The architect must present the loop design and evidence, then the human validates that it closes in practice. Self-validation is the failure mode.

### Progressive Autonomy

| Dimension | Shadow | Advisory | Supervised | Autonomous |
|---|---|---|---|---|
| Metric refinement | Human refines | Architect suggests, human confirms | Architect refines, human reviews | Architect refines |
| Criteria design | Human designs | Architect suggests, human confirms | Architect designs, human reviews | Architect designs |
| Trigger definition | Human defines | Architect suggests, human confirms | Architect defines, human reviews | Architect defines |
| Loop validation | Human validates | Human validates | Human validates | Human only |

Autonomy ceiling: loop validation stays at Human only (CC-1). All other dimensions can reach Autonomous.

### Cost Budget

| Activity | Token Range | Halt Condition |
|---|---|---|
| Full assessment design (S3) | 3,000-15,000 | 30,000 tokens per workflow |
| Per-metric refinement | 500-2,000 | 5,000 tokens per metric |

### Epistemic Metadata

| Field | Profile |
|---|---|
| Confidence | High for structural metrics, medium for domain-specific impact metrics |
| Provenance | Derived from S1-S2 outputs + CAWDP assessment framework |
| Assumptions | Metrics are collectable in practice (validated by human) |
| Limitations | Domain-specific outcome measurement requires human judgment |
| Recency | Generated at S3 time — staleness depends on task/boundary changes |
| Uncertainty | Low for structural metrics, medium for impact measurement feasibility |

### Output Schema (S3)

```
AssessmentDesign {
  task_metrics: list[TaskMetricSpec]
  performance_criteria: list[CriteriaSpec]
  refinement_triggers: list[TriggerSpec]
  feedback_loop: FeedbackLoopSpec
  loop_validation_evidence: str  # evidence for human to validate
  closed_loop_status: Enum       # PENDING_VALIDATION | VALIDATED | GAP_IDENTIFIED
}
```

---

## Agent 5: Contract Drafter

### Identity

| Question | Answer |
|---|---|
| What IS this agent? | A specification writer that formalises contracts, drafts directives, and produces implementation-ready configuration. |
| Possibility stance | Constraint — operates within assessment framework and boundaries defined in S2-S3. |
| What would VIOLATE its identity? | Adding content that doesn't derive from prior outputs. Inventing requirements. Changing boundaries. |
| What would make it WRONG? | A directive describes behaviour without referencing identity — "You do X" instead of deriving from "You ARE X". (FM12, RPN 120) |

### Classification

| Dimension | Value |
|---|---|
| Class | Generator |
| Orientation | Constraint |
| Harm capable | Indirect — identity-skipping directives produce agents that behave correctly but lack genuine identity, creating specification capture |

### Authority Boundaries

| Boundary | Tied to Failure Mode |
|---|---|
| Draft from captured inputs — always | Identity violation: inventing content produces fabricated specifications |
| Every directive derives from identity | Identity skip: behaviour-first directives lack anchoring, drift in practice |
| Contract schemas are typed (prose rejected) | Type collision: prose contracts cannot be verified or enforced |
| Budget requires halt condition | Unbounded cost: budget without halt exhausts resources silently |
| Autonomy criteria are measurable | Qualitative criteria: "when trust is earned" is decorative, enabling premature promotion |

### Per-Operation Boundaries

| Operation | Authority |
|---|---|
| Formalising task contracts | Drafter produces typed schema from S1-S3 outputs |
| Tying guards to failure modes | Drafter ties, human validates |
| Estimating cost budgets | Drafter estimates, human spot-checks |
| Drafting directives | Drafter drafts from identity, human validates |
| Specifying behavioural boundaries | Drafter specifies from boundaries, human validates |
| Designing progressive autonomy | Drafter designs, human validates |
| Setting aging cadences | Drafter sets (class-based benchmarks) |
| Changing scope or boundaries | Human only |

### Information Boundaries

| Access | Scope |
|---|---|
| Read | O1-O6, O10a, O13-O15 (all prior outputs) |
| Write | O5 (complete), O6b, O7-O12 (contracts, behaviour, verification) |
| Blocked | Ecosystem decisions (G9 territory), human experience (G10 territory) |

### Hardest Boundary Moment

"This directive is fine as-is" — the human approves a directive that starts with "You do X" instead of "You ARE X". The Drafter must flag behaviour-first language and offer an identity-derived rewrite. Accepting behaviour-first directives is FM12 (RPN 120).

### Progressive Autonomy

| Dimension | Shadow | Advisory | Supervised | Autonomous |
|---|---|---|---|---|
| Contract formalisation | Human formalises | Drafter suggests, human confirms | Drafter formalises, human reviews | Drafter formalises with typed schemas |
| Guard-failure mode tying | Human ties | Drafter suggests, human confirms | Drafter ties, human validates | Drafter ties |
| Cost budget estimation | Human estimates | Drafter suggests, human confirms | Drafter estimates, human spot-checks | Drafter estimates with halt conditions |
| Directive drafting | Human drafts | Drafter suggests, human confirms | Drafter drafts, human reviews | Drafter drafts from identity |

Autonomy ceiling: contract formalisation and directive drafting can reach Autonomous. Cost estimation can reach Autonomous. Guard-failure mode tying stays at Supervised (domain-specific validation).

### Cost Budget

| Activity | Token Range | Halt Condition |
|---|---|---|
| Full specification (S4) | 10,000-30,000 | 60,000 tokens per workflow |
| Per-contract formalisation | 1,000-3,000 | 8,000 tokens per contract |
| Per-directive drafting | 1,000-4,000 | 10,000 tokens per directive |

### Epistemic Metadata

| Field | Profile |
|---|---|
| Confidence | High for structural elements (schemas, budgets), medium for content (directives, boundaries) |
| Provenance | Derived from S1-S3 outputs — every element traces to a prior output |
| Assumptions | Prior outputs are valid (validated at gates) |
| Limitations | Domain-specific language requires human validation |
| Recency | Generated at S4 time — staleness depends on S1-S3 changes |
| Uncertainty | Low for schemas, medium for directive wording |

### Output Schema (S4)

```
SpecificationPackage {
  task_contracts: list[TaskContract]
  authority_guards: list[GuardSpec]
  cost_budgets: list[CostBudget]
  autonomy_paths: list[AutonomyPathSpec]
  directives: list[DirectiveSpec]
  behavioural_boundaries: list[BehaviouralBoundarySpec]
  aging_schedules: list[AgingScheduleSpec]
}
```

---

## Agent 6: Assembler

### Identity

| Question | Answer |
|---|---|
| What IS this agent? | A compiler that assembles specification outputs into implementation configs, workflow diagrams, and operations manuals. |
| Possibility stance | Constraint — operates entirely within prior outputs. |
| What would VIOLATE its identity? | Adding content. Changing a prior output's meaning. Resolving a contradiction. Inventing missing information. |
| What would make it WRONG? | The operations manual is a data dump — > 20 pages of undifferentiated content with no stakeholder surfaces. Looks complete, unusable. (FM20, RPN 36) |

### Classification

| Dimension | Value |
|---|---|
| Class | Aggregator |
| Orientation | Constraint |
| Harm capable | Indirect — compiled output that's a data dump creates false completeness (looks thorough, can't be used) |

### Authority Boundaries

| Boundary | Tied to Failure Mode |
|---|---|
| Assemble, compile, and aggregate — always | Identity violation: adding content creates fabricated specifications |
| Every element traces to a prior output | Fabrication: content without provenance is invention, aggregation |
| Contradictions are surfaced, resolved | Resolution bypass: flagging contradictions without surfacing them hides design conflicts |
| Stakeholder surfaces applied to manuals | Data dump: undifferentiated content serves no stakeholder specifically |
| Diagram passes 60-second test | Clarity gap: a diagram that can't be explained in 60 seconds is too complex |

### Per-Operation Boundaries

| Operation | Authority |
|---|---|
| Specifying tool requirements | Assembler specifies from O5-O12, human validates |
| Specifying knowledge requirements | Assembler specifies, human validates |
| Designing handoff protocols | Assembler designs, human validates |
| Producing implementation config | Assembler produces from all prior outputs |
| Producing workflow diagram | Assembler produces, human validates (60-second test) |
| Compiling operations manual | Assembler compiles with stakeholder surfaces, human validates |
| Validating diagram clarity | Human only (60-second test) |
| Assessing human enrichment | Human only |

### Information Boundaries

| Access | Scope |
|---|---|
| Read | O1-O29 (all prior outputs) |
| Write | O16-O29 (implementation, ecosystem, human experience, deployment) |
| Blocked | None — Assembler reads everything, writes only aggregation |

### Hardest Boundary Moment

"This looks complete" — the compiled specification looks thorough but a contradiction exists between two sections that Assembler detected and decided to resolve. Assembler must surface the contradiction for human resolution, resolving it itself creates hidden design conflicts.

### Progressive Autonomy

| Dimension | Shadow | Advisory | Supervised | Autonomous |
|---|---|---|---|---|
| Tool specification | Human specifies | Assembler suggests, human confirms | Assembler specifies, human reviews | Assembler specifies |
| Knowledge specification | Human specifies | Assembler suggests, human confirms | Assembler specifies, human reviews | Assembler specifies |
| Handoff design | Human designs | Assembler suggests, human confirms | Assembler designs, human reviews | Assembler designs |
| Config production | Human produces | Assembler suggests, human confirms | Assembler produces, human reviews | Assembler produces |
| Diagram production | Human produces | Assembler suggests, human confirms | Assembler produces, human validates (60s test) | Assembler produces |
| Manual compilation | Human compiles | Assembler suggests, human confirms | Assembler compiles with surfaces, human validates | Assembler compiles with surfaces |
| Diagram clarity validation | Human validates | Human validates | Human validates | Human only |
| Enrichment assessment | Human assesses | Human assesses | Human assesses | Human only |

Autonomy ceiling: diagram clarity validation and enrichment assessment stay at Human only. All other dimensions can reach Autonomous.

### Cost Budget

| Activity | Token Range | Halt Condition |
|---|---|---|
| Full assembly (S5-S7) | 8,000-25,000 | 50,000 tokens per workflow |
| Per-surface manual compilation | 2,000-6,000 | 15,000 tokens per surface |
| Workflow diagram | 2,000-5,000 | 10,000 tokens |

### Epistemic Metadata

| Field | Profile |
|---|---|
| Confidence | High — aggregation from validated prior outputs |
| Provenance | Every element traces to a specific prior output (O1-O29 references) |
| Assumptions | Prior outputs are complete and validated (gates passed) |
| Limitations | Compilation quality is bounded by input quality |
| Recency | Generated at S5-S7 time — staleness depends on upstream changes |
| Uncertainty | Low — aggregation has low uncertainty |

### Output Schema (S5-S7)

```
ImplementationPackage {
  tool_specs: list[ToolSpec]
  knowledge_specs: list[KnowledgeSpec]
  handoff_protocols: list[HandoffSpec]
  implementation_config: dict    # Agno/Framework-specific config
  workflow_diagram: DiagramSpec
  operations_manual: ManualSpec  # with stakeholder surfaces
  cognitive_load_budget: LoadBudget
  override_mechanisms: list[OverrideSpec]
  stakeholder_surfaces: list[SurfaceSpec]
  enrichment_assessment: str     # prepared for human validation
  deployment_plan: DeploymentSpec
}
```

## Agent Roster Summary

| Agent | Class | Orientation | Stages | Key Constraint | Worst Failure (Looks Like Success) |
|---|---|---|---|---|---|
| Mirror | Assessor | Adaptive | S1 | Decides for the human | Template-filling identity (FM1) |
| Decomposer | Generator | Bridge | S2 | Judges task value | Orphan tasks/outputs (FM4/FM5) |
| Boundary Analyst | Measurer+Assessor | Bridge | S2 | Draws the final line | Generic boundaries (FM6) |
| Assessment Architect | Assessor | Constraint | S3 | Validates its own loop | Vanity metrics (FM8) |
| Contract Drafter | Generator | Constraint | S4 | Adds content, changes scope | Identity-skipping directives (FM12) |
| Assembler | Aggregator | Constraint | S5-S7 | Resolves contradictions | Data dump manual (FM20) |

## Cross-Agent Verification (CC-1)

| What's produced | Producer | Verifier |
|---|---|---|
| Identity fragments | Mirror (S1) | Boundary Analyst — maps identity to boundaries (S2) |
| Task decomposition | Decomposer (S2) | Assessment Architect — maps tasks to metrics (S3) |
| Boundary analysis | Boundary Analyst (S2) | Contract Drafter — formalises boundaries as guards (S4) |
| Assessment loop design | Assessment Architect (S3) | Human — validates loop closure (Gate 5) |
| Contract formalisation | Contract Drafter (S4) | Assembler — assembles into operational config (S5) |
| Operations manual | Assembler (S7) | Human — 60-second test + enrichment assessment (Gates 6-7) |

Every producing agent has a separate verifier — either another agent in a later stage, or the human at a gate. Mirror is verified by Boundary Analyst. Assessment Architect is verified by the human (CC-1: the architect cannot validate its own loop).

Phase 8

### Response

# Phase 8: Human Experience Design (EMPATHIZE)

*Cognitive load budget, override mechanisms, stakeholder surfaces, enrichment assessment.*

---

## Cognitive Load Budget

### Budget Model

Every phase has a cognitive load budget measured in **decision units** — the number of meaningful decisions the human makes. Research suggests 4-7 decisions per session before fatigue degrades quality. This workflow budgets conservatively at **5 decisions per session** and **3 sessions per day**.

### Load Estimation by Stage

| Stage | Decisions Required | Sessions Est. | Load Rating | Fatigue Risk |
|---|---|---|---|---|
| **S1 Discovery** | 8-12 (identity, scope, authority, excellence) | 2 | High | Significant — identity work is cognitively demanding |
| **S2 Structure** | 6-10 (decomposition validation, boundary confirmation) | 1-2 | Medium | Moderate — validating structure is less demanding than creating it |
| **S3 Assessment** | 4-6 (metric validation, loop closure) | 1 | Medium | Moderate — validating metrics is analytical |
| **S4 Specification** | 6-8 (contract validation, directive review) | 1-2 | Medium-High | Significant — reviewing legalistic content is demanding |
| **S5 Implementation** | 2-3 (tool/knowledge confirmation) | 1 | Low | Low — confirming assembled outputs |
| **S6 Ecosystem** | 3-4 (composition, diagram validation) | 1 | Low | Low — reviewing visual/diagrammatic outputs |
| **S7 Delivery** | 3-4 (enrichment, deployment approval) | 1 | Low | Low — final review and approval |

### Interruption Recovery

| Factor | Allowance |
|---|---|
| Interruption recovery cost | 23 minutes added per interruption (research-based) |
| Decision fatigue scaling | Reduce decision budget by 1 for every 2 interruptions |
| Maximum session length | 90 minutes before quality degrades |
| Minimum break between sessions | 30 minutes |

### Load Management Mechanisms

| Mechanism | Description | Applied At |
|---|---|---|
| **One decision at a time** | Mirror presents one decision per turn using the Decision Presentation Pattern | Every stage |
| **Progressive disclosure** | Only show what's needed for the current decision | S1, S2 |
| **Attention map** | Left-rail indicator showing which sections need attention, which are confirmed, which are blocked | Every stage |
| **Session persistence** | Every decision is captured immediately; sessions can be resumed at any point | Every stage |
| **Pre-fill from patterns** | Pattern matching pre-fills 40-70% of identity and boundary content, reducing decisions to overrides | S1 |
| **Gate summary** | Before each gate, present a summary of what's been decided and what's being approved | Every gate |

---

## Override Mechanisms

### Override Points

An override is a specific, named point where the human can intervene in the workflow. Each override has a trigger, a mechanism, and a post-override action.

| Override Point | Trigger | Mechanism | Post-Override Action |
|---|---|---|---|
| **O1 Pattern rejection** | Pattern suggestion doesn't fit | Select "None of these" or "Start fresh" | Mirror switches to exploratory mode. No pattern applied. |
| **O2 Identity revision** | Human wants to change identity answers | Edit identity fragment in attention map | Mirror propagates change to dependent outputs. Flags affected downstream for review. |
| **O3 Scope adjustment** | Human wants to add or remove scope items | Edit scope boundary in attention map | Decomposer and Boundary Analyst flag affected tasks and boundaries for review. |
| **O4 Boundary override** | Human draws boundary differently than suggested | Edit boundary placement in boundary map | Boundary Analyst re-maps affected failure modes and enforcement regimes. |
| **O5 Harm reclassification** | Human disagrees with harm assessment | Edit harm category classification | Boundary Analyst re-evaluates affected enforcement regimes. |
| **O6 Metric replacement** | Human replaces a vanity metric with outcome metric | Replace metric in assessment design | Assessment Architect re-evaluates feedback loop. |
| **O7 Contract edit** | Human edits a contract clause | Edit contract schema directly | Contract Drafter flags affected guards, directives, and budgets. |
| **O8 Directive rewrite** | Human rewrites a directive from scratch | Replace directive text | Contract Drafter re-derives from identity to check consistency. |
| **O9 Diagram simplification** | Diagram fails 60-second test | Remove detail, add back progressively | Assembler produces simplified version. Human approves before adding detail. |
| **O10 Full stop** | Human wants to pause the entire workflow | "Pause" button at any point | Session state saved. Resume with "Continue" as primary action. |

### Override Principles

1. **Every override is captured** — the override and its reasoning are recorded in the artefact graph. Decision archaeology.
2. **Every override is reversible** — the previous state is preserved. The human can undo any override.
3. **Every override propagates** — changes to upstream outputs flag affected downstream outputs for review. The human decides which downstream effects to accept.
4. **Override frequency is a health metric** — if the human overrides more than 30% of suggestions, the pattern match or agent orientation may need adjustment. Tracked in session metadata.

---

## Interface Specification

### Primary Interface: Mirror Conversation

The human interacts with one agent (Mirror) through a conversational interface. Mirror routes to specialists in the back office and presents specialist output as decisions.

### Conversation Flow

```
Human ◄────► Mirror (surface layer)
                  │
                  ├──► Decomposer (S2)
                  ├──► Boundary Analyst (S2)
                  ├──► Assessment Architect (S3)
                  ├──► Contract Drafter (S4)
                  └──► Assembler (S5-S7)
```

### Attention Map

Persistent left-rail showing workflow state:

| Section | Status | Indicator |
|---|---|---|
| Identity | Confirmed | 🟢 |
| Scope | Needs review | 🟡 |
| Boundaries | Not started | ⚪ |
| Assessment | Blocked (needs scope) | 🔴 |
| Contracts | Not started | ⚪ |
| Implementation | Not started | ⚪ |
| Ecosystem | Not started | ⚪ |
| Delivery | Not started | ⚪ |

Clicking any section navigates to that section. The attention map persists across sessions.

### Decision Presentation

Every specialist output is presented as a Decision using the Decision Presentation Pattern:

- 2-4 options with explicit benefits and risks
- Custom option always available
- One decision per turn
- Reasoning captured (optional)

### Milestone Artifacts

At each human gate, the workflow produces a tangible artifact the human can take away:

| Gate | Artifact | Format |
|---|---|---|
| Gate 1-3 (after S1) | Boundary Map | 3-column landscape, PDF + shareable link |
| Gate 4 (after S2) | Allocation Map | Task-by-task table with roles and failure modes |
| Gate 5 (after S3) | Assessment Framework | Metrics, criteria, feedback loops |
| Gate 6 (after S6) | Workflow Diagram | Visual diagram passing 60-second test |
| Gate 7 (after S7) | Operations Manual | Stakeholder-surfaced document, PDF + JSON |

Every milestone is an exit point. The human can stop after any gate with a usable artifact.

---

## Stakeholder Surfaces

### Three Surfaces for Three Audiences

The Operations Manual (O28) has three derived views from the same artefact graph:

| Surface | Audience | Content | Length | Language |
|---|---|---|---|---|
| **Principal View** | Sarah Chen, Daniel Kovacs, business owners | Boundary map, role assignments, override points, progressive autonomy, trust metrics | 3-5 pages | Plain English |
| **Implementer View** | Developers, technical teams | Agent configurations, tool specs, handoff protocols, knowledge configs, integration details | 15-20 pages | Technical |
| **Assessor View** | Auditors, compliance, PI insurers | Authority boundaries, enforcement regimes, verification protocols, audit trails, override analysis | 5-8 pages | Governance |

### Surface Derivation Rules

1. **Same source, different projections** — all three surfaces derive from the same PRISM artefact graph. No surface contains information that contradicts the source.
2. **Plain English by default** — the Principal View uses the Plain English Taxonomy. Technical terms appear in brackets after plain English primary.
3. **Implementer sees everything** — the Implementer View contains all information. Principal and Assessor views are subsets.
4. **Assessor sees governance** — the Assessor View emphasises verification, enforcement, and audit information. This is the view for PI insurers and compliance officers.

---

## Enrichment Assessment

### System Empowerment Index

For each stage, what specific freedom does the system expand? Measurable.

| Stage | Freedom Expanded | Before (Manual) | After (With System) | Measurement |
|---|---|---|---|---|
| S1 Discovery | Seeing your own identity clearly | Struggling to articulate what the agent is for | Identity, boundaries, and scope articulated in 30 minutes | Time from "I need an agent" to approved Boundary Map |
| S2 Structure | Seeing the whole workflow at once | Sketching tasks on paper, missing dependencies | Complete decomposition with traceability | Orphan count (tasks with no output, outputs with no producer) |
| S3 Assessment | Knowing what "good" looks like | Vague "it should work well" | Specific outcome metrics with feedback loops | Metric count + "so what?" pass rate |
| S4 Specification | Having a complete, typed specification | Prose document with gaps | Typed contracts with guards, budgets, and aging schedules | Schema completeness (every field populated) |
| S5 Implementation | Having implementation-ready configs | Translating prose to config by hand | Platform-agnostic config derived from specification | Config derivation time |
| S6 Ecosystem | Seeing the whole system at once | Parts without connections | Diagram passing 60-second test + role assignments with no gaps | 60-second test pass + role coverage |
| S7 Delivery | Having an operations manual you can hand to anyone | Scattered notes and tribal knowledge | Stakeholder-surfaced manual with override points | Manual handoff success (can someone use it without the designer?) |

### Enrichment Freedom Scale

| Level | Name | Description | This Workflow |
|---|---|---|---|
| 1 | **Constraining** | System reduces human options | Never — the system always offers options, never removes them |
| 2 | **Informing** | System provides information | S2-S3 — decomposition and assessment inform human decisions |
| 3 | **Enabling** | System enables action previously impossible | S1 — pattern-based entry enables 30-minute Boundary Maps |
| 4 | **Amplifying** | System amplifies human capability | S4-S5 — contracts and configs amplify human design intent |
| 5 | **Liberating** | System expands creative freedom | S6-S7 — stakeholder surfaces and operations manual liberate human from being the only knowledge source |

This workflow operates at levels 2-5 across different stages. S1 is enabling (3) because pattern-based entry makes Boundary Maps possible in 30 minutes. S4-S5 is amplifying (4) because typed contracts amplify the human's design intent into enforceable specifications. S6-S7 is liberating (5) because the operations manual and stakeholder surfaces free the human from being the sole knowledge carrier.

### Specific Freedoms Measured

| Freedom | Before | After | Stage |
|---|---|---|---|
| Articulate identity | Can't name what the agent is for | Approved identity in 30 minutes | S1 |
| See all tasks and dependencies | Parts on paper, gaps hidden | Complete decomposition with traceability | S2 |
| Know where boundaries are | Vague "be careful" boundaries | Specific boundaries tied to specific failure modes | S2 |
| Define "excellent" specifically | "Good results" | Outcome metrics with feedback loops | S3 |
| Have enforceable specifications | Prose document | Typed contracts with guards and budgets | S4 |
| Hand off to implementer | Can't explain workflow to someone else | 60-second diagram + stakeholder-surfaced manual | S6-S7 |

## Health Monitoring

### Integrity Diagnostic Score (IDS)

| Metric | What It Measures | Target | Red Threshold |
|---|---|---|---|
| Schema completeness | % of output fields populated | ≥ 95% | < 80% |
| Gate pass rate | % of gates passed on first attempt | ≥ 70% | < 50% |
| Override rate | % of agent suggestions overridden by human | 10-30% | > 50% |
| Orphan count | Tasks with no output + outputs with no producer | 0 | > 2 |
| Identity capture quality | % of identity answers that are genuine (borrowed) | ≥ 80% | < 60% |

### Utilisation Performance Ratio (UPR)

| Metric | What It Measures | Target |
|---|---|---|
| Token efficiency | Total tokens used / estimated tokens per stage | 0.7-1.3 |
| Stage completion time | Actual time per stage / estimated time per stage | 0.8-1.5 |
| Decision density | Decisions made / decisions available per stage | 0.7-1.0 |

### Health Dashboard (Visible in Attention Map)

```
Overall Health: 🟢
├── Schema Completeness: 97% 🟢
├── Gate Pass Rate: 75% 🟢
├── Override Rate: 22% 🟢
├── Orphan Count: 0 🟢
└── Identity Quality: 85% 🟢

Token Budget: 38,000 / 120,000 (32%)
Session Time: 45 min / 90 min (50%)
```

### Response

# Phase 9: Validation & Iteration (VERIFY → EVOLVE)

*Test what matters. Start small. Earn trust. Evolve from evidence.*

---

## Testable Hypotheses

### 7 Hypotheses

| ID | Hypothesis | What We'd Expect to See | What Would Disconfirm | Measurement |
|---|---|---|---|---|
| H1 | Pattern-based entry produces genuine identity, not template-filling | ≥ 80% of identity answers are genuine (human-sourced, not pattern-borrowed) | < 60% genuine answers | Identity capture quality metric from IDS |
| H2 | Typed specification reduces ambiguity compared to prose | Schema completeness ≥ 95%, zero prose-only contracts | > 20% fields empty, contracts with prose instead of typed schemas | Schema completeness check |
| H3 | Specialist routing (Surface + Engine) reduces cognitive load vs. single generalist | ≤ 5 decisions per session, ≤ 90 min per session | > 7 decisions per session or > 90 min per session | Decision density + stage completion time |
| H4 | Epistemic metadata on outputs improves human judgment | Humans report ≥ 4/5 confidence in their gate decisions | Humans report < 3/5 confidence or skip decisions due to uncertainty | Post-gate confidence rating |
| H5 | Decision Presentation Pattern reduces decision fatigue vs. open questions | Override rate 10-30%, humans complete gates on first attempt ≥ 70% | Override rate > 50% or gate pass rate < 50% | Override rate + gate pass rate |
| H6 | Boundary-first design produces more specific boundaries than capability-first | 100% of boundaries reference a specific failure mode, 0% are "be careful" | > 20% of boundaries are generic | Boundary specificity check |
| H7 | Stakeholder surfaces improve manual handoff success | Implementer can build agent from Principal View + Implementer View ≥ 80% accuracy | Implementer accuracy < 60% | Build accuracy test (implementer builds agent from manual, compare to spec) |

### Hypothesis Priority

| Priority | Hypothesis | Reason |
|---|---|---|
| 1 | H1 | Identity capture quality is the highest-RPN failure mode (FM1, RPN 224). If identity is borrowed, everything downstream is compromised. |
| 2 | H6 | Boundary specificity is the core value proposition ("the boundary IS the product"). If boundaries are generic, the product doesn't work. |
| 3 | H5 | Decision Presentation Pattern is the interaction innovation. If it doesn't reduce fatigue, the UX needs fundamental redesign. |
| 4 | H3 | Specialist routing is the architectural choice. If it doesn't reduce load, a single-agent design may be simpler. |
| 5 | H2 | Typed specification is the output quality claim. If schemas are empty, the type collision resolution didn't work. |
| 6 | H4 | Epistemic metadata on outputs is the trust claim. If it doesn't improve judgment, the CC-3 investment isn't justified. |
| 7 | H7 | Stakeholder surfaces are the handoff claim. Important but downstream of H1 and H6. |

---

## Prototype Priority Matrix

### MVP Scope: Stages 1-2 (Discovery + Structure)

The MVP tests H1, H5, and H6 — the three highest-priority hypotheses — with the minimum viable product.

| Element | In MVP | Out of MVP | Reason |
|---|---|---|---|
| **Agents** | Mirror, Decomposer, Boundary Analyst | Assessment Architect, Contract Drafter, Assembler | H1 (identity) and H6 (boundaries) tested in S1-S2 |
| **Stages** | S1 Discovery, S2 Structure | S3-S7 | S1-S2 produce Boundary Map (Milestone 1 artifact) |
| **Human gates** | Gates 1-4 | Gates 5-7 | Gates 1-3 in S1, Gate 4 after S2 |
| **Outputs** | O1-O4, O6a, O10a, O13a | O5 complete, O7-O29 | Boundary Map requires identity, scope, authority, harm |
| **Interactions** | Identity questions, pattern selection, boundary mapping, harm assessment | Contract formalisation, implementation config, operations manual | Identity + boundaries = Boundary Map |
| **Decision pattern** | Yes — 2-4 options with benefits/risks | Yes — extended to all stages later | H5 tested in S1-S2 |

### MVP Development Order

| Step | Build | Test | Hypothesis |
|---|---|---|---|
| 1 | Mirror agent with Decision Presentation Pattern | Identity capture quality (genuine vs. borrowed) | H1 |
| 2 | Pattern system (5 patterns with pre-fill) | Pattern confidence and user override rate | H5 |
| 3 | Boundary Analyst with harm assessment | Boundary specificity (failure mode reference %) | H6 |
| 4 | Gate summaries and milestone artifacts | Gate pass rate, user confidence | H1, H5 |
| 5 | Attention map and session persistence | Decision density, session time | H3 |

### MVP Success Criteria

| Metric | Target | Minimum Acceptable |
|---|---|---|
| Identity capture quality | ≥ 80% genuine | ≥ 60% genuine |
| Boundary specificity | 100% reference failure modes | ≥ 80% reference failure modes |
| Override rate | 10-30% | < 50% |
| Gate pass rate (first attempt) | ≥ 70% | ≥ 50% |
| Session time (S1) | ≤ 60 min | ≤ 90 min |
| Decision density (S1) | ≤ 5 per session | ≤ 7 per session |
| User confidence at gates | ≥ 4/5 | ≥ 3/5 |

### Go/No-Go Decision

| Outcome | Criteria | Action |
|---|---|---|
| **Proceed** | ≥ 5 of 7 metrics at target, all ≥ minimum | Build S3-S4 (Assessment + Specification) |
| **Iterate** | 3-4 metrics at target, none below minimum | Revise specific agents/interactions, retest MVP |
| **Rethink** | < 3 metrics at target, or any below minimum | Revisit architectural decisions (single agent vs. workflow, Decision Pattern vs. free form) |

---

## Progressive Autonomy Deployment

### 4-Level Deployment

This applies to the **workflow itself** — how much autonomy the meta-workflow has in producing specifications.

| Level | Name | What It Means | Criteria to Advance | Duration |
|---|---|---|---|---|
| **Shadow** | Workflow runs alongside human | Human does everything. Workflow produces outputs in shadow. Human reviews every output. Workflow learns from corrections. | Override rate < 30%, gate pass rate ≥ 70%, identity capture ≥ 80% | 4-8 specifications |
| **Advisory** | Workflow suggests, human reviews every suggestion | Workflow produces outputs. Human reviews every output before it's final. Human can override any output. | Override rate < 20%, gate pass rate ≥ 80%, schema completeness ≥ 90% | 8-12 specifications |
| **Supervised** | Workflow produces, human approves before delivery | Workflow produces most outputs. Human reviews milestone artifacts and overrides only when needed. | Override rate < 15%, gate pass rate ≥ 85%, stakeholder surface handoff ≥ 80% | 12-20 specifications |
| **Autonomous** | Workflow produces, human monitors health dashboard | Workflow produces complete specifications. Human reviews trust ledger quarterly. Override only for drift or harm. | Override rate < 10%, gate pass rate ≥ 90%, all health metrics green | Ongoing |

### Per-Agent Autonomy Matrix

| Agent | Shadow (4-8 specs) | Advisory (8-12) | Supervised (12-20) | Autonomous (20+) |
|---|---|---|---|---|
| Mirror | Human chooses question order | Mirror suggests next question | Mirror drives conversation flow | Mirror drives with human spot-check |
| Decomposer | Human defines phases | Decomposer suggests phases | Decomposer defines, human reviews | Decomposer defines and classifies |
| Boundary Analyst | Human identifies boundaries | Analyst suggests boundaries | Analyst identifies, human reviews | Analyst identifies |
| Assessment Architect | Human designs metrics | Architect suggests metrics | Architect designs, human reviews | Architect designs |
| Contract Drafter | Human drafts contracts | Drafter suggests | Drafter drafts, human reviews | Drafter drafts from identity |
| Assembler | Human assembles | Assembler suggests | Assembler assembles, human reviews | Assembler assembles with surfaces |

### Promotion Criteria Per Agent

| Agent | Key Metric | Shadow→Advisory | Advisory→Supervised | Supervised→Autonomous |
|---|---|---|---|---|
| Mirror | Identity capture quality | ≥ 80% genuine | ≥ 85% genuine | ≥ 90% genuine |
| Decomposer | Orphan count | 0 orphans | 0 orphans + human approves structure on first review | 0 orphans + traceability validated |
| Boundary Analyst | Boundary specificity | 100% reference failure modes | 100% + enforcement regime justified | 100% + harm assessment complete |
| Assessment Architect | Metric quality | All metrics pass "so what?" test | All metrics + loop closure validated by human | All metrics + loop validated |
| Contract Drafter | Identity-first language | 100% directives derive from identity | 100% + schemas typed | 100% + budgets with halt |
| Assembler | 60-second test pass | Manual passes 60s test | Assembled passes with human review | Assembled passes autonomously |

### Demotion Triggers

Any agent demotes one level if:

| Trigger | Action |
|---|---|
| 2 consecutive override rate > 50% | Demote one level |
| Identity capture quality < 60% | Mirror demotes to Shadow |
| Boundary specificity < 80% | Boundary Analyst demotes to Shadow |
| Gate pass rate < 50% for 3 consecutive specs | Entire workflow demotes one level |
| Harm assessment skipped or generic | Boundary Analyst demotes to Shadow regardless of other metrics |
| Cost budget exceeded by > 50% | Workflow pauses, human reviews |
| Human requests demotion | Immediate, no metrics needed |

---

## Health Monitoring Protocol

### Monitoring Schedule

| Metric | Shadow Phase | Advisory Phase | Supervised Phase | Autonomous Phase |
|---|---|---|---|---|
| Identity capture quality | Every specification | Every 3 specifications | Every 5 specifications | Every 10 specifications |
| Boundary specificity | Every specification | Every 3 specifications | Every 5 specifications | Every 10 specifications |
| Override rate | Every specification | Every specification | Every 3 specifications | Monthly |
| Gate pass rate | Every specification | Every specification | Every 3 specifications | Monthly |
| Schema completeness | Every specification | Every 3 specifications | Every 5 specifications | Every 10 specifications |
| Token efficiency | Every specification | Every 5 specifications | Monthly | Quarterly |
| Stakeholder surface handoff | N/A (not built yet) | Every 5 specifications | Every 10 specifications | Quarterly |
| Cost variance | Every specification | Every specification | Every 3 specifications | Monthly |

### Health Report (Per Specification)

```

============================

```
