| User experience modifier | Progressive disclosure level | 0.8 (Quick Start) → 1.0 (Practitioner) → 1.3 (Architect) |
| Session sequence modifier | Position in Boundary Journey | 0.7 (first session — unfamiliar) → 1.0 (second session — pattern recognized) → 1.2 (third+ — routine) |
| Decision complexity modifier | Average decision complexity in this session | 0.6 (high complexity — identity questions) → 1.0 (standard) → 1.4 (low complexity — status review) |

**Sample Calculations:**

| User | Domain | Session | Budget |
|---|---|---|---|
| Sarah Chen (novice) | High-stakes legal | First Boundary Map | 5 × 0.7 × 0.8 × 0.7 × 0.6 = **1.2 → 1-2 decisions** |
| Daniel Kovacs (Practitioner) | Standard legal | Second Allocation Map | 5 × 1.0 × 1.0 × 1.0 × 1.0 = **5 decisions** |
| Peter (Architect) | Low-stakes operational | Fifth Trust Ledger | 5 × 1.3 × 1.3 × 1.2 × 1.4 = **14 → 12-15 decisions** |

Sarah Chen's first session should have **1-2 decisions**, not 5. That means the Mirror Agent presents fewer options per turn and spreads the identity questions across more turns.

**Implementation Architecture:**

```
cognitive_load_calculator/
  ├── models.py          # CognitiveLoadBudget, SessionProfile, DecisionProfile Pydantic models
  ├── calculator.py      # Budget calculation engine
  ├── session_tracker.py # Tracks decisions made per session, adjusts modifier over time
  ├── domain_profiles.py # Default domain weight profiles
  └── api.py             # API for integration with Design Studio and Mirror Agent
```

**Integration Points:**

| Integration | What It Does |
|---|---|
| Mirror Agent | Uses budget to pace decisions per turn |
| Design Studio | Displays remaining decision capacity in attention map |
| Trust Ledger | Tracks decision fatigue indicators (rushing, rubber-stamping, inconsistency) |
| Progressive Autonomy | Decision budget increases as user gains experience (learning scaffold) |

**Connection to existing concepts:** This operationalizes CC-2 (Human Enrichment Assessment) and ADHD design principle #1 (Cognitive Load as a Budget). The budget is literally a budget — a finite resource that must be allocated. The calculator makes the budget adaptive rather than fixed. It connects to the User Context Framework (cognitive style, time constraints, decision complexity all influence the budget).

---

### 2.3 Pattern Library with Validation Pipeline

**The Problem**

The 5 patterns (Signal Detector, Multi-Lens Analyst, Discovery Explorer, Learning Scaffold, Review Partner) are theoretical. They pre-fill 40-70% of the specification based on accumulated design knowledge, but they've never been validated against real specifications produced by real users.

The retrospective identified that pattern-first entry is "the hardest innovation to replicate" because it requires accumulated design knowledge. But that knowledge is currently in Peter's head, not in a system.

**The Solution**

Build a **Pattern Library** with a validation pipeline that turns real specifications into refined patterns over time:

**Pattern Structure (expanded):**

```
Pattern:
  identity:
    name: "Review Partner"
    class: Assessor
    orientation: Constraint
    description: "Reviews work products against defined criteria, never finalizes"
    
  pre_fills:
    identity_questions:
      Q1: "A quality gatekeeper that reviews work against criteria"
      Q2: "Stay in Lane"  # constraint-oriented
      Q3: ["Approve without verification", "Skip edge cases", "Accept at face value"]
      Q4: "Plausible-but-wrong acceptance"  # worst failure looks like success
      
    boundaries:
      you_column: ["Final approval", "Exception handling", "Policy interpretation"]
      agent_column: ["Evidence extraction", "Criteria matching", "Gap identification"]
      system_column: ["Schema validation", "Audit trail", "Status tracking"]
      
    progressive_autonomy:
      dimensions:
        - name: "Criteria matching"
          ceiling: Supervised
          reason: "Boundary cases require human judgment"
        - name: "Evidence extraction"
          ceiling: Autonomous
          reason: "Mechanical once criteria established"
        - name: "Gap identification"
          ceiling: Supervised
          reason: "Unknown unknowns require domain expertise"
          
    contract_primitives:  # Pre-filled for P8
      guard_defaults: ["onlyHumanAuthority(final_approval)", "prohibited(skip_verification)"]
      revert_defaults: ["per_output", "reject_and_flag"]
      budget_defaults: ["5000_tokens_per_review", "halt_on_exhaustion"]
      
  validation:
    specifications_derived_from: 0  # How many real specs used this pattern
    override_rate: null  # How often users overrode pre-fills
    completion_time: null  # Average time to complete spec with this pattern
    user_satisfaction: null  # Post-session rating
    
  confidence_thresholds:
    high: 80  # 80%+ match → 60-70% pre-fill
    medium: 60  # 60-79% → 40-50% pre-fill
    low: 40  # 40-59% → 20-30% pre-fill
    no_match: 0  # Below 40% → exploratory mode
```

**Validation Pipeline:**

```
Real Specification → Pattern Extraction → Pattern Comparison → Pattern Refinement

Step 1: User completes specification (with or without pattern match)
Step 2: System extracts structural features:
  - Agent class, orientation, identity answers
  - Boundary placement, never-rules, hardest boundary moment
  - Progressive autonomy dimensions and ceilings
  - Contract primitives and enforcement regimes
Step 3: Compare extracted features against existing patterns:
  - High match (>80%): Add to pattern's validation count
  - Partial match (40-80%): Flag as potential pattern extension
  - Low match (<40%): Flag as potential new pattern
Step 4: Refine patterns based on accumulated data:
  - Override rates indicate where pre-fills are wrong
  - Completion times indicate where complexity is excessive
  - Satisfaction scores indicate where the pattern helps vs hinders
```

**Implementation Architecture:**

```
pattern_library/
  ├── models.py          # Pattern, PatternMatch, ValidationResult Pydantic models
  ├── matcher.py         # Pattern matching engine (input → pattern confidence)
  ├── extractor.py       # Structural feature extraction from completed specs
  ├── validator.py       # Validation pipeline (compare, refine, suggest)
  ├── library.py         # Pattern storage and retrieval
  └── api.py             # API for integration with Design Studio and Mirror Agent
```

**New Pattern Discovery:**

After 20+ specifications, the Pattern Library should surface new patterns organically. If 5+ specifications share structural features not captured by existing patterns, the system proposes a new pattern. The contributor (Architect-level user) reviews, refines, and publishes it.

This is the **community flywheel** from the opinionated framework recasting: Convention → Practitioners → Patterns → Trust Data → Convention.

**Connection to existing concepts:** This is "convention over configuration" operationalized. The Pattern Library IS the "15-minute agent specification" — selecting a pattern pre-fills the specification so the user only fills in what's unique about their agent. It connects to the Red Hat model (open patterns, commercial certification of pattern expertise) and to the CAWDP Design Studio (pattern-first entry as the onboarding experience).

---

### 2.4 Specification Quality Gate Engine

**The Problem**

CAWDP defines 5 quality gates with 3 layers each (Fidelity/Enrichment/Cross-Cutting), but the gates are currently procedural descriptions, not executable checks. The human reviewer must manually verify that each gate condition is met. This is error-prone and inconsistent.

The Schema Quality Gate (SQG) demonstrated that automated quality checks catch problems humans miss (2 silent data loss patterns, 6 correction patterns). The same principle should apply to CAWDP quality gates.

**The Solution**

Build a **Quality Gate Engine** that executes quality gate checks programmatically:

**Gate Structure:**

```python
class QualityGate:
    phase: int
    name: str
    checks: list[GateCheck]
    
class GateCheck:
    id: str  # e.g., "P7-F-01" (Phase 7, Fidelity layer, Check 1)
    layer: Literal["fidelity", "enrichment", "cross_cutting"]
    description: str
    check_type: Literal["exists", "complete", "consistent", "traceable", "enforced"]
    query: str  # Query against the PRISM artefact graph
    pass_criteria: str  # What "pass" looks like
    fail_action: Literal["block", "warn", "flag"]  # What happens on failure
```

**Example Checks by Phase:**

| Phase | Layer | Check | Query | Pass Criteria | Fail Action |
|---|---|---|---|---|---|
| P0 | Fidelity | All 4 dimensions have characteristics | `count(dimensions) == 4` | Each dimension has 5+ characteristics | Block |
| P1 | Fidelity | Every output has schema, dependencies, quality gate | `forall(outputs, has_schema AND has_deps AND has_gate)` | 100% coverage | Block |
| P2 | Fidelity | No circular dependencies in output chain | `no_cycles(dependency_graph)` | Acyclic graph | Block |
| P4 | Fidelity | Human-only tasks have gap ≥ 6 | `forall(allocations, gap >= 6 → allocation == "human")` | Consistent | Block |
| P7 | Enrichment | Hardest boundary moment has enforcement regime | `exists(boundary_moment AND enforcement_regime)` | Specified | Warn |
| P8 | Fidelity | Every ● cell in 10×10 matrix completed | `forall(mapping_cells, status != "empty")` | 100% | Block |
| P8 | Enrichment | Unenforceable elements documented | `count(unenforceable) >= 0 AND all_documented` | Documented | Warn |
| P8 | Cross-cutting | Contract verifier ≠ specification author | `verifier != author` | Different agents | Block |

**Implementation Architecture:**

```
quality_gate_engine/
  ├── models.py          # QualityGate, GateCheck, GateResult Pydantic models
  ├── engine.py          # Gate execution engine
  ├── queries/           # TypeQL/SQL queries for each check
  │   ├── p0_queries.tql
  │   ├── p1_queries.tql
  │   └── ...
  ├── reporter.py        # Gate result reporting (text, JSON, SARIF)
  └── api.py            # API for Design Studio integration
```

**Integration with Design Studio:**

The Quality Gate Engine runs after each phase completion. Results appear in the attention map:
- 🟢 Passed: no action needed
- 🟡 Warning: should address before next phase
- 🔴 Blocked: must address before proceeding

This doesn't replace human judgment at the gates — it automates the mechanical checks so the human can focus on the design decisions.

**Connection to existing concepts:** This is the SQG concept (37 checks for TypeQL schema) generalized to the entire CAWDP process. Each quality gate check is a typed, structured, traceable artifact — the same type collision resolution principle applied to quality assurance.

---

### 2.5 Decision Fatigue Detector

**The Problem**

Cognitive load budgeting (improvement 2.2) sets the budget, but doesn't detect when the budget is exceeded. If a user is making too many decisions too quickly, or rubber-stamping decisions without genuine judgment, the specification quality degrades. This is FM1 (identity template-filling, RPN 224) — the highest risk in the meta-application.

The current system has no mechanism to detect decision fatigue or rubber-stamping.

**The Solution**

Build a **Decision Fatigue Detector** that monitors decision patterns in real-time:

**Detection Signals:**

| Signal | What It Indicates | Detection Method |
|---|---|---|
| Decision velocity | Decisions per minute exceeding budget | Time between decisions |
| Rubber-stamping | Accepting defaults without modification | Override rate tracking |
| Consistency drift | Contradictory decisions across questions | Cross-reference checking |
| Engagement decline | Decreasing time spent on each decision | Time-on-task tracking |
| Language shift | Moving from domain-specific to generic language | Vocabulary analysis |
| Rush signals | "That's fine" / "Whatever works" / "Sure" | Acceptance language patterns |

**Response Protocol:**

| Fatigue Level | Signals | Response |
|---|---|---|
| **Green** (normal) | Decision velocity within budget, override rate 10-40%, consistent decisions | Continue session |
| **Amber** (fatigued) | Decision velocity 1.5× budget, override rate >60% or <5%, minor inconsistencies | Mirror suggests a break: "You've made some important decisions. Would you like to save your progress and continue another time, or keep going?" |
| **Red** (impaired) | Decision velocity 2× budget, override rate >80% or <2%, significant contradictions | Mirror pauses: "I'm noticing some patterns that suggest you might be running low on decision energy. Your specification will be stronger if you come back fresh. Save and continue?" |

**Critical Design Decision:** The Mirror can **suggest** a pause, but never **force** one. The human is the principal. The agent prepares the judgment (detecting fatigue); the human makes the decision (whether to pause).

**Implementation:**

This is a feature of the Mirror Agent, not a separate tool. The fatigue signals are computed from session state (decision timestamps, override counts, content analysis). The response is a conversational prompt, not a system block.

**Connection to existing concepts:** This directly addresses FM1 (identity template-filling) — the highest-risk failure mode. Rubber-stamping IS template-filling in real-time. The detector operationalizes ADHD design principle #1 (Cognitive Load as a Budget) at the session level. It connects to the Decision Presentation Pattern (fewer options reduce decision fatigue) and to progressive disclosure (revealing complexity gradually reduces cognitive load).

---

### 2.6 Feasibility Contamination Checker

**The Problem**

The P0-P2 feasibility contamination review found that ~36% of Phase 0 characteristics contained mechanism contamination — mixing HOW (implementation mechanisms) with WHAT (ideals). "Quasi-smart contracts," "Agno," and "typed schemas" are mechanisms, not ideals.

The Possibility Orientation Principle says P0-P2 should be possibility-oriented (ideals, framework-neutral, implementation-agnostic). But even the methodology's designer couldn't avoid this contamination without the principle explicitly named and enforced.

**The Solution**

Build a **Feasibility Contamination Checker** that scans specification text for mechanism keywords and flags potential contamination:

**Contamination Detection Rules:**

| Category | Flag Keywords | What They Indicate |
|---|---|---|
| Framework references | "Agno", "LangChain", "CrewAI", "AutoGen" | Implementation-specific, not framework-neutral |
| Infrastructure references | "Postgres", "TypeDB", "Chroma", "Docker", "Cloudflare" | Implementation-specific, not infrastructure-neutral |
| Pattern references | "quasi-smart contract", "MCP", "ERC-4337" | Implementation-specific, not pattern-neutral |
| Language references | "Python", "TypeScript", "SQL", "TQL" | Implementation-specific, not language-neutral |
| Architecture references | "microservice", "monorepo", "serverless" | Implementation-specific, not architecture-neutral |

**Two-Pass Check:**

1. **Keyword scan** — flags any specification text in P0-P2 that contains mechanism keywords
2. **Semantic check** — for each flagged item, asks: "Is this describing WHAT the agent should be (ideal) or HOW it should be implemented (mechanism)?"

**Resolution:**

For each contamination detected:
- **Separate:** Extract the mechanism into a "Mechanism Notes" section (belongs in P3+)
- **Replace:** Rewrite the characteristic as an ideal (framework-neutral statement)
- **Document:** Record the contamination and its resolution in the transformation log

**Example:**

| Contaminated | Clean |
|---|---|
| "Uses TypeDB for typed knowledge graph" | "Knowledge is typed, connected, and navigable" |
| "Deployed on Agno AgentOS" | "Runs on an agent runtime with session persistence" |
| "Stores data in quasi-smart contracts" | "Every boundary is enforceable at the system level" |
| "Uses Pydantic schemas for validation" | "Input and output schemas are structurally validated" |

**Implementation:**

This is a feature of the Quality Gate Engine (improvement 2.4), not a separate tool. It runs as a P0-P2 specific check:

```python
class FeasibilityContaminationCheck(GateCheck):
    phase = 0  # Also runs for P1, P2
    layer = "fidelity"
    check_type = "consistent"
    description = "P0-P2 characteristics are framework-neutral ideals, not mechanisms"
    query = "scan_for_mechanism_keywords(phase_characteristics)"
    pass_criteria = "Zero mechanism keywords in P0-P2"
    fail_action = "warn"  # Not blocking — human decides
```

**Connection to existing concepts:** This directly operationalizes the Possibility Orientation Principle (CC-9). P0-P2 = possibility-oriented. P3+ = progressively constraint-oriented. The checker enforces the boundary between possibility and feasibility at the text level. It's the same principle as the SQG's S02 rule (role name collision with entity types) — catching type collision at the structural level before it causes problems downstream.

---

## Section 3: Design Pattern Codification

### 3.1 Surface + Engine Pattern

**The Pattern**

One user-facing agent (Surface) routes to multiple specialist agents (Engine). The user interacts with one conversation. The system routes to the right specialist based on context.

**Codification:**

```
Surface Agent:
  Class: Assessor
  Orientation: Adaptive (shifts with context)
  Identity: "I reflect and route, never decide or execute"
  Authority: Present options, explain routing, capture decisions
  Never: Execute specialist tasks, filter options, skip routing
  
Engine Agents:
  Class: Per specialist (varies)
  Orientation: Per specialist (varies with phase position)
  Identity: Per specialist (varies)
  Authority: Per specialist boundaries
  Never: Per specialist boundaries
  
Routing Logic:
  - Phase-based: route to specialist matching current CAWDP phase
  - Content-based: route to specialist matching task type
  - Ambiguity: route to most conservative specialist (doubt defaults to human)
  
CC-1 Enforcement:
  - Surface agent ≠ any engine agent
  - Producing specialist ≠ verifying specialist
  - Surface doesn't verify; engine doesn't surface
```

**When to Use:** Any multi-specialist workflow where the user should interact with one agent, not manage multiple conversations.

**Anti-Pattern:** Surface + Engine where the Surface agent makes decisions about what the engine should produce. The Surface reflects; the Engine executes. If the Surface decides, it violates its identity.

---

### 3.2 Milestone-as-Exit Pattern

**The Pattern**

Every phase boundary produces a standalone valuable artifact. Users can exit at any milestone with something they can use, not a partial specification.

**Codification:**

```
Milestone:
  gate: int  # Which human gate
  artifact: str  # What the user takes away
  value_statement: str  # Why it's independently valuable
  exit_optionality: str  # What the user can do with it independently
  
  Examples:
    Gate 1-3 → Boundary Map: "Know where the line is"
      → Take to any vendor, implement yourself, or continue
    Gate 4 → Allocation Map: "Know who does what"
      → Brief any team, assign roles, or continue
    Gate 7 → Operations Manual: "Know it's governed"
      → Give to insurer, auditor, or continue
```

**When to Use:** Any workflow where the user may not complete all phases, or where partial completion should still deliver value.

**Anti-Pattern:** Milestones that require the next milestone to be useful. "This allocation map only works if you also have the operations manual" = dead end, not exit.

---

### 3.3 Possibility Gradient Pattern

**The Pattern**

The workflow starts expansive (possibility-oriented) and tightens toward constraint. Each phase narrows the space of legitimate questions.

**Codification:**

```
Possibility Gradient:
  P0-P2: EXPANSIVE — ask "what could be?", reject feasibility language
  P3-P5: CONSTRUCTIVE — ask "what should be?", introduce feasibility
  P6-P8: CONSTRAINED — ask "what must be?", enforce structure
  P9: REOPENS — ask "how does this feel?", partially expansive
  P10: SPIRALS — ask "what needs to change?", closes back to P0

Per-Phase Failure Mode:
  P0-P2: Qualifying possibility (shouldn't narrow yet)
  P3-P5: Ignoring feasibility (shouldn't stay expansive)
  P6-P8: Reopening possibility (shouldn't expand again)
  P9: Being purely constraint (shouldn't stay constrained)
  P10: Declaring success (shouldn't close without evolution path)
```

**When to Use:** Every CAWDP application. The gradient is structural, not cosmetic.

**Anti-Pattern:** Asking feasibility questions in P0 ("what framework should we use?") or possibility questions in P8 ("what else could this boundary be?"). The gradient should be enforced, not optional.

---

### 3.4 Contract Depth Scaling Pattern

**The Pattern**

Contract formalization depth scales with agent class and autonomy level. Simple agents get shallow contracts. Complex agents get deep contracts.

**Codification:**

```
Contract Depth by Agent Class:
  Extractor (Shadow): 2 of 10 primitives (Schema, Event)
  Measurer (Supervised): 3 of 10 (Schema, Event, Guard)
  Assessor (Supervised): 4 of 10 (Schema, Event, Guard, Principal)
  Generator (Autonomous): 10 of 10 + full enforcement regime map
  Aggregator (Autonomous): 10 of 10 + cross-agent contract integration

Contract Depth by Autonomy Level:
  Shadow: Minimum primitives (Schema, Event only)
  Advisory: Add Guard
  Supervised: Add Principal, Budget
  Autonomous: All 10 + enforcement regime map
```

**When to Use:** Phase 8 (Contract Formalization). Not every agent needs a 10-primitive contract. Scale the work to the stakes.

**Anti-Pattern:** Writing a full 10-primitive contract for an Extractor running in Shadow mode. This is over-engineering that wastes time and creates maintenance burden without proportional value.

---

### 3.5 Identity-to-Enforcement Cascade Pattern

**The Pattern**

Identity questions produce authority boundaries, which produce enforcement regimes, which produce contract primitives. The cascade is directional and traceable.

**Codification:**

```
Cascade:
  Q1 (What IS it?) → Agent class → Contract Identity primitive
  Q2 (Possibility stance?) → Orientation → Enforcement regime target
  Q3 (What VIOLATES identity?) → Never-rules → Guard primitives
  Q4 (What makes it WRONG?) → Failure modes → Revert + Event primitives
  Q5 (Hardest boundary moment?) → Stress test → Highest-priority Guard

Traceability:
  Every Guard traces to Q3 or Q5 (which identity violation it prevents)
  Every Revert traces to Q4 (which failure mode it addresses)
  Every Event traces to Q4 or Q5 (which failure or boundary it signals)
  Every Budget traces to Q5 (which boundary moment it limits)
```

**When to Use:** Phase 7 → Phase 8 transition. The specification-to-contract transformation follows this cascade.

**Anti-Pattern:** Writing Guard primitives without tracing them to identity violations. If a Guard can't answer "which identity violation does this prevent?", it's not derived from the specification — it's invented.

---

## Section 4: Integration Architecture

### 4.1 How the Tools Compose

The five tooling improvements (Backcasting Engine, Cognitive Load Calculator, Pattern Library, Quality Gate Engine, Decision Fatigue Detector, Feasibility Contamination Checker) compose into a single system:

```
┌─────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────┐
│                    CAWDP DESIGN STUDIO                       │
│                                                              │
│  ┌──────────┐  ┌──────────┐  ┌──────────┐  ┌──────────┐    │
│  │ Pattern  │  │Backcast  │  │ Quality  │  │ Cognitive│    │
│  │ Library  │  │ Engine   │  │ Gate     │  │ Load     │    │
│  │          │  │          │  │ Engine   │  │ Calc     │    │
│  └────┬─────┘  └────┬─────┘  └────┬─────┘  └────┬─────┘    │
│       │              │              │              │          │
│       ▼              ▼              ▼              ▼          │
│  ┌──────────────────────────────────────────────────────┐   │
│  │              MIRROR AGENT (Surface)                   │   │
│  │  Pattern matching · Decision pacing · Fatigue detect  │   │
│  └──────────────────────────────────────────────────────┘   │
│                                                              │
│  ┌──────────────────────────────────────────────────────┐   │
│  │           SPECIALIST AGENTS (Engine)                  │   │
│  │  Decomposer · Boundary Analyst · Assessment Architect │   │
│  │  Contract Drafter · Assembler                         │   │
│  └──────────────────────────────────────────────────────┘   │
│                                                              │
│  ┌──────────────────────────────────────────────────────┐   │
│  │           PRISM ARTEFACT GRAPH (Single source)        │   │
│  │  Specification surface · Contract surface · Ops surface│   │
│  └──────────────────────────────────────────────────────┘   │
└─────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────┘
```

**Data flow:**

1. User enters → Pattern Library matches → Mirror Agent receives pattern + pre-fills
2. Mirror asks identity questions → Cognitive Load Calculator sets decision budget → Fatigue Detector monitors
3. Specialist agents produce artefacts → Quality Gate Engine checks → PRISM Graph stores
4. Contract Drafter formalizes → Backcasting Engine traces dependencies → Quality Gate validates completeness
5. Feasibility Contamination Checker scans P0-P2 → flags mechanism keywords → human decides

---

### 4.2 Implementation Priority

| Priority | Tool | Reason | Estimated Effort |
|---|---|---|---|
| **1** | Pattern Library (core 5 patterns) | Enables 15-minute specification, validates with 5 real users | 2-3 weeks |
| **2** | Cognitive Load Calculator (basic) | Prevents FM1 (highest risk), enables adaptive pacing | 1-2 weeks |
| **3** | Quality Gate Engine (P7-P8 only) | Validates specification-to-contract transformation, enforces CC-1 | 2-3 weeks |
| **4** | Decision Fatigue Detector | Addresses FM1 in real-time, integrates with Mirror Agent | 1-2 weeks |
| **5** | Backcasting Engine | Automates P2, highest mechanical complexity | 3-4 weeks |
| **6** | Feasibility Contamination Checker | Enforces CC-9 at text level, prevents P0-P2 contamination | 1 week |
| **7** | Pattern Library (validation pipeline) | Community flywheel, requires 20+ specifications to be useful | 4-6 weeks |
| **8** | Quality Gate Engine (full P0-P10) | Complete coverage, requires all phase queries written | 4-6 weeks |

**Recommended build order:** 1 → 2 → 4 → 6 → 3 → 5 → 7 → 8

The first four tools (Pattern Library, Cognitive Load Calculator, Fatigue Detector, Contamination Checker) can be built in 5-8 weeks and directly support the MVP: testing the Boundary Map with 5 real users.

---

## Section 5: Summary of All Changes

### Methodology Structure Changes (5)

| # | Change | CAWDP Phase Affected | Priority |
|---|---|---|---|
| 1.1 | Hardest boundary moment as 5th identity question | P0, P7, P8 | High |
| 1.2 | Per-dimension progressive autonomy as default | P7 | High |
| 1.3 | Null-state output as universal hard constraint | P7, P8 | Medium |
| 1.4 | Two-category harm assessment (direct + indirect) | P7 | Medium |
| 1.5 | Enforcement regime specification for every boundary | P7, P8 | High |

### Process and Tooling Improvements (6)

| # | Improvement | Phase Served | Build Priority | Effort |
|---|---|---|---|---|
| 2.1 | Backcasting Engine | P2 | 5 | 3-4 weeks |
| 2.2 | Cognitive Load Budget Calculator | P9 | 2 | 1-2 weeks |
| 2.3 | Pattern Library with validation pipeline | P0, P7 | 1, 7 | 2-3 + 4-6 weeks |
| 2.4 | Quality Gate Engine | All | 3, 8 | 2-3 + 4-6 weeks |
| 2.5 | Decision Fatigue Detector | All sessions | 4 | 1-2 weeks |
| 2.6 | Feasibility Contamination Checker | P0-P2 | 6 | 1 week |

### Design Pattern Codification (5)

| # | Pattern | When to Use | Anti-Pattern |
|---|---|---|---|
| 3.1 | Surface + Engine | Multi-specialist workflows | Surface decides |
| 3.2 | Milestone-as-Exit | Any workflow with exit points | Milestones require next milestone |
| 3.3 | Possibility Gradient | Every CAWDP application | Feasibility in P0, possibility in P8 |
| 3.4 | Contract Depth Scaling | P8 Contract Formalization | Full contract for Shadow Extractor |
| 3.5 | Identity-to-Enforcement Cascade | P7 → P8 transition | Guards without identity trace |

### Total: 16 Changes

- 5 methodology structure changes (can be implemented in template revisions)
- 6 tooling improvements (require development, prioritized by MVP support)
- 5 design pattern codifications (documentation, no development needed)

---

## The One Thing That Matters Most

16 improvements. 5 methodology changes. 6 tools. 5 patterns. The report is thorough.

But the retrospective said the same thing the methodology says: **the next step is not more methodology.**

The most important improvement is **testing the Boundary Map with 5 real people**. Everything else — the 5 methodology changes, the 6 tools, the 5 patterns — is preparation for that test. If the Boundary Map doesn't produce relief in 30 minutes, none of the other improvements matter. If it does, every improvement here makes the next iteration better.

The Pattern Library (core 5 patterns) and the Cognitive Load Calculator (basic) directly support the Boundary Map test. Build those first. Test with 5 people. Then decide what to build next based on what you learn.

The methodology says: **five conversations, not five more designs.**The full report is above. 16 improvements organized into three categories, with build priorities and the honest conclusion: the most important next step isn't building any of these — it's five conversations with real people using the Boundary Map.

That said, if you want to start building, the Pattern Library and Cognitive Load Calculator are the two tools that directly support the Boundary Map test. Everything else can come after you've validated the core hypothesis.

What would you like to explore next?
